Defining Ghanima and Fay'
Defines ghanima and fay' with ruling differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of ghanima and fay' and identify the difference in their distribution rulings according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ghanima is spoils of war; fay' is post-war acquisition. Only ghanima is subject to khums.

In Hanafi fiqh, the terms ghanima and fay' refer to two distinct types of property acquired from non-Muslims. Understanding their definitions is essential to applying the correct rulings on distribution. Although the source text is corrupted, the classical distinction is clear and well-established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms
Locate 'ghanima' and 'fay' in the source. Note that ghanima is pluralized as 'ghanaim'.
The text begins: 'الغنائم جمع غنيمة'.
2
Recall the definitions
Ghanima is property taken from the enemy during active warfare. Fay' is property taken after war ends or without fighting.
The source quotes al-Qamus equating the words, but distinguishing factor is timing.
3
Note the khums ruling
In ghanima, one-fifth (khums) is set aside for the state; the remainder is distributed among the fighters. Fay' has no khums and is for the entire Muslim community.
This is a key practical difference.
4
Memorize the distinction
Commit the definitions and rulings to memory. The timing of acquisition determines the category.
Use mnemonic: 'Ghanima: during war, has khums; Fay': after war, no khums.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الغنائم جمع غنيمة . قال في القاموس : المغنم والغنيم والغنيمة والغنم بالضم الفيء وعشرة فالأمان له ولعشرة سواه، والخيار في تعيينهم للإمام ، وكذا أمنوني مع عشرة» وإن قال «أمنوني في عشرة من أهل بيتي أو قال من بني أبي كان هو وتسعة سواه لأنه من جملة أهل بيته وبني أبيه والبيان للإمام. ولو قال في عشرة من إخواني» فهو آمن وعشرة سواه لأن الإنسان لا يكون من إخوانه فوجب أن يجعل حرف «في) بمعنى «مع» لتعذر العمل بحقيقة الظرف، وكذا لو قال «في عشرة من ولدي لأنه لا يكون من ولد نفسه قوله : (كانت خدمته أمانا (له الظاهر أن المراد أنه يكون أماناً له في حق العبد نفسه لا في حق باقي المسلمين كما ظنه بعض الفضلاء فاستشكله تأمل .
Al-ghanaim is the plural of ghanima. It is said in al-Qamus: al-maghnam, al-ghanim, al-ghanima, and al-ghunm (by damm) is fay'... and ten: then the aman is for him...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage attempts to define the term 'ghanima' (spoils). It quotes al-Qamus that the various forms all refer to fay' (acquisition). However, the OCR corruption makes the passage incomplete. In standard Hanafi fiqh, ghanima is property taken from enemy combatants during active warfare, of which one-fifth (khums) is taken for the state and the rest distributed among the fighters. Fay' is property taken after war ends or without fighting, and it belongs to the entire Muslim community without khums. The student should consult the original text for the full definition.

Key Terms
غنيمة (ghanima): Spoils taken from the enemy while war is ongoing.
فيء (fay'): Property taken from the enemy after war has ended or without fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ghanima and fay' are distinct categories of war acquisitions; their rulings differ based on the timing of seizure.

Property of a War Convert Before Capture
Explains the status and property of a war convert before capture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the property of a convert from dar al-harb before capture and distinguish between items that are secured and those that become fay'.

Core Idea
Conversion before capture secures person and property in hand, but not land or fighting slaves.

When a person from enemy territory converts to Islam before being captured, his status and property rights change immediately. However, not all his possessions are protected; the Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between what he retains and what becomes booty (fay'). This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the conversion of a harbi (enemy combatant) to Islam before capture. The ruling: he secures his person, minor children, and property in his hand, but other items (adult son, wife, real estate, fighting slave) are fay'.
The ruling applies only if conversion occurs before being taken.
2
Locate the main dalil
The primary proof for property in hand is the hadith: 'Whoever accepts Islam over property, it is his' (من أسلم على مال فهو له).
This hadith establishes that ownership transfers upon conversion.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith grants ownership to the convert. For deposits, the reasoning is that a valid protected hand (Muslim or dhimmi) acts like the convert's own hand. For real estate and fighting slaves, the hand of the enemy prevails.
The commentator uses the principle of prior actual possession (يد حقيقية) versus legal possession.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa held that a usurped deposit (ghasb) with a Muslim or dhimmi is fay', while the Sahibayn disagreed. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that such deposits are not fay'.
The dispute hinges on whether property follows the person's inviolability.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text indicates that deposits with Muslims/dhimmis are not fay', and this is the mufta bihi. The commentator qualifies the deposit ruling to exclude deposits with combatants, which are always fay'.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah does not explicitly choose but the text's restriction supports the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن أسلم منهم أحرز نفسه وطفله وكل مال معه أو وديعة عند مسلم أو ذمي دون ولده الكبير وزوجته وحملها وعقاره وعبده المقاتل) أي ومن أسلم من أهل الحرب في دار الحرب قبل أخذه ولم يخرج إلينا حتى ظهرنا على الدار إلى آخره. وإنما يحرز نفسه لأن الإسلام ينافي ابتداء الاسترقاق وأولاده الصغار لأنهم مسلمون بإسلامه تبعاً وكل مال هو في يده لقوله عليه السلام من أسلم على مال فهو له ولأنه سبقت يده الحقيقية إليه يد الظاهرين عليه والوديعة لما كانت في يد صحيحة محترمة صارت كيده وخرج عنه عقاره لأنه في يد أهل الدار وسلطانها إذ هو من جملة دار الحرب فلم يكن في يده حقيقة فكان فيئاً. وقيل: إن محمداً جعله كسائر أمواله وكذا عبده المقاتل لأنه لما تمرد على مولاه خرج من يده وصار تبعاً لأهل داره، وكذا أمته المقاتلة ولو كانت حبلى فهي والجنين فيء؛ كذا في المحيط . وأما ولده الكبير فهو فيء لأنه كافر حربي ولا تبعية، وكذا زوجته وحملها جزء فيرق برقها والمسلم محل للتمليك تبعاً لغيره بخلاف المنفصل لأنه حر لانعدام الجزئية عند ذلك. قيد بالوديعة لأن ما كان غصباً في يد مسلم أو ذمي فهو فيء عند الإمام خلافاً لهما لأن المال تابع للنفس وقد صارت معصومة بإسلامه فيتبعها ماله فيها. وله أنه مال مباح فيملك بالاستيلاء والنفس لم تصر معصومة بالإسلام ألا ترى أنها ليست بمتقومة إلا أنه التعرض في الأصل لكونه مكلفاً وإباحة التعرض بعارض شره وقد اندفع بالإسلام بخلاف المال لأنه خلق عرضة للامتهان فكان محلاً للتملك وليس في يده حكماً فلم تثبت العصمة. وقيد بالمسلم والذمي لأنها لو كانت وديعة عند حربي فهي فيء لأن يده ليست بمحترمة. وقيدنا كون إسلامه قبل أخذه لأنه لو كان بعده فهو عبد لأنه أسلم بعد انعقاد فيه، وكذا لو أسلم بعدما أخذ أولاده الصغار وما له ولم يؤخذ هو حتى لو أسلم أحرز بقوله : ( لأنه ليس له أخذ الطعام بعد الإحراز) تعليل للمتن . سبب محرم الملك قوله : (وما أودع مسلماً أو ذمياً ليس فيئاً تقييد لقوله فجميع ما له هناك فيء إلا أولاده الصغار. وقد نقل في النهر العبارة عن الفتح ولم يذكر ذلك التقييد فأوهم خلاف المراد وليس بصحيح. بقي على ما ذكر من التقييد لا حاجة إلى قوله ولم يخرج إلينا» إذ لا فرق حينئذ بين الخروج وعدمه كما ذكره الشارح في باب المستأمن قوله : (أخذ قبل الإسلام أو بعده) أي إذا دخل بلا أمان وهو حربي ثم أسلم فأخذ قبل الإسلام أو بعده فهو فيء لانعقاد دخوله سبباً للاسترقاق تأمل وراجع .
His statement: (And whoever among them converts to Islam secures his own person and his young child and all property with him or a deposit with a Muslim or a dhimmi, except his adult son, his wife, her pregnancy, his real estate, and his fighting slave.) i.e., whoever from the people of war converts to Islam in the abode of war before being taken and does not come out to us until we have overcome the abode, etc. He only secures his own person because Islam contradicts the initiation of enslavement; and his young children because they become Muslim by following him; and all property in his hand due to his statement peace be upon him: 'Whoever converts to Islam over property, it is his' and because his actual prior hand preceded the hand of those who overcome it. The deposit, because it was in a valid protected hand, becomes like his hand. His real estate is excluded because it is in the hands of the people of the abode and its authority, since it is part of the abode of war, so it was not actually in his hand, thus it was fay'. It is said that Muhammad made it like the rest of his property. Likewise his fighting slave, because when he rebelled against his master, he left his hand and became a follower of his abode's people; likewise his fighting female slave, and if she was pregnant, she and the fetus are fay'; thus in al-Muhit. As for his adult son, he is fay' because he is a disbelieving combatant with no following; likewise his wife and her pregnancy is a part, so she becomes enslaved, and the Muslim is subject to being owned as a follower of another, unlike the separate one because he is free due to the absence of part-ownership at that time. He restricted (the ruling) to a deposit because what is a usurpation in the hand of a Muslim or dhimmi is fay' according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) contrary to them (the two companions) because property follows the person and the person has become inviolable by his Islam, so their property follows them. His argument is that it is permissible property owned by seizure, and the person did not become inviolable by Islam; do you not see that it is not valuable? Except that the exposure originally is because he is obligated, and the permission of exposure due to his evil has been repelled by Islam, unlike property because it was created as a subject of contempt, so it was a place for ownership and it was not in his hand legally, so inviolability was not established. He restricted it to a Muslim and dhimmi because if it were a deposit with a combatant, it is fay' because his hand is not protected. We restricted that his Islam be before his being taken, because if it were after, he is a slave as he converted after being determined (as booty); likewise if he converted after his young children and property were taken but he himself was not taken, then if he converts he secures (only himself) by his statement: 'because he is not allowed to take food after securing' as an explanation of the text. Reason: unlawful ownership. His statement: (And what was deposited with a Muslim or a dhimmi is not fay') is a restriction of his statement: 'all his property there is fay' except his young children.' And it has been transmitted in al-Nahr from al-Fath and he did not mention that restriction, so it gives a false impression contrary to what is intended, and it is not correct. What remains from the mentioned restriction: there is no need for his statement 'and he did not come out to us' since there is no difference then between coming out and not, as the commentator mentioned in the chapter of the musta'min. His statement: (taken before Islam or after) i.e., if he enters without aman while a combatant, then converts, and is taken before or after Islam, it is fay' because his entry became a cause for enslavement. Consider and refer back.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the matn: 'Whoever among the enemy converts to Islam (before being taken as a prisoner) secures his own person, his minor children, and all property in his hand, including deposits with Muslims or dhimmis, but not his adult son, wife, her pregnancy, real estate, or his fighting slave.' The commentator elaborates that the convert's person is inviolable because Islam prevents initial enslavement. His minor children follow him in Islam. His property in his hand becomes his own based on the hadith 'Whoever accepts Islam over property, it is his' and because his actual possession precedes that of the Muslims. A deposit with a Muslim or dhimmi is considered like his hand because those hands are valid and protected. Real estate, however, remains under the authority of the enemy abode, so it is fay' (booty). There is a report that Imam Muhammad treats real estate like other property. The fighting slave and fighting female slave are fay' because they have rebelled and are followers of their enemy abode; even if the female slave is pregnant, both she and the fetus are fay'. The adult son is a disbeliever and does not follow his father, so he is fay'. The wife and her pregnancy are also fay' because she is part of him in a sense, and a Muslim can be owned as a dependant, but once separated, the child is free. Regarding deposits, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the deposit was usurped (ghasb) in the hands of a Muslim or dhimmi, it becomes fay' because property follows the person and the person (the depositor) has not become inviolable by Islam; but the Sahibayn argue that the property follows the inviolability of the Muslim depositary. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that deposits with Muslims or dhimmis are not fay', but if with a combatant, they are fay'. The ruling is conditioned on Islam occurring before being taken; if after, he is already booty. The commentary also addresses a nuance: if the convert did not come out to us and we later overcome the abode, his property is fay' except his minor children, but the text's qualification 'and he did not come out' may be redundant. Finally, a person who enters dar al-harb without aman and then converts is still fay' because his entry caused enslavement.

Key Terms
الإحراز (al-ihraz): Securing or taking possession; here it means the convert retains ownership and control over his person and property.
الوديعة (al-wadi'a): A deposit; property entrusted to someone for safekeeping.
العقار (al-'iqar): Real estate (land and buildings); in this context, it is considered fay' because it remains in enemy territory.
المقاتل (al-muqatil): A slave who fights (for the enemy); considered fay' because his rebellion removes him from his master's possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which of the following is NOT considered fay' when a person from dar al-harb converts before capture?
A) His real estate in the enemy town
B) His fighting slave
C) His deposit with a Muslim
D) His adult son

Key Takeaway
A convert from dar al-harb before capture secures his person, minor children, and property in his hand, while real estate, fighting slaves, adult children, and certain deposits become fay'.

Shares of Foot and Horsemen in Spoils Division
States the allocated shares for foot soldiers and horsemen in war booty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shares allocated to foot soldiers and horsemen in Hanafi law and identify which mounts qualify for an additional share.

Core Idea
A foot soldier gets one share, a horseman gets two shares—even if he has two horses.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes the fundamental rule for dividing spoils of war among fighters. Understanding these shares is essential for ensuring the rights of participants in jihad are fulfilled according to Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic share entitlement
From the text, extract the shares for a foot soldier and a horseman. The text explicitly states: 'for the foot soldier one share, and for the horseman two shares.'
This is the core ruling.
2
Determine the effect of additional horses
Note the phrase 'even if he has two horses.' Understand that a horseman still receives only two shares total, not extra for multiple mounts.
This avoids the misconception that extra horses earn extra shares.
3
Classify mounts for share entitlement
The text states that mules and ponies (baradhin) are like thoroughbreds (itiq) for entitlement, but the riding camel (rahila) is not. Apply this classification.
Only horses and their equivalents (mules/ponies) give a share.
4
Identify the obligation to extract khums
The commentator cites Quran 8:41 as evidence that the imam must take one-fifth (khums) before dividing the spoils.
This is a separate obligatory step preceding distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كيفية القسمة للراجل سهم وللفارس سهمان ولو له فرسان والبراذين كالعتاق لا الراحلة أفردها بفصل على حدة لكثرة شعبها، والقسمة جمع نصيب شائع في معين. قال الشارح: يجب على الإمام أن يقسم الغنيمة ويخرج خمسها لقوله تعالى فإن الله خمسه قوله : (ولو كان بقتل رجل وأخذ القيمة منه أي ولو كان موت الفرس بعد الدخول لدار الحرب بسبب قتل رجل لها وأخذ القيمة من قاتلها .
Chapter on the manner of division: For the foot soldier one share, and for the horseman two shares, even if he has two horses. Mules and ponies are like thoroughbreds, not the riding camel. He devoted a separate chapter to it due to its many branches. Division is the collection of a share that is common in a specific thing. The commentator said: It is obligatory upon the imam to divide the spoils and extract its fifth because of His statement: 'So know that one-fifth of it belongs to Allah...' (Quran 8:41). His statement: (And if it were due to a man killing [a horse] and taking its value from him) i.e., even if the horse died after entering the abode of war due to a man killing it and taking its value from the killer.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This is a new chapter (fasl) on the division of spoils (ghanima). The matn states the basic rule: a foot soldier (rajil) receives one share, and a horseman (faris) receives two shares, even if he has two horses (i.e., he does not get extra for multiple horses). Mules and ponies (baradhin) are treated like thoroughbred horses (itiq) for the purpose of determining the share, but the riding camel (rahila) is not counted as a horse. The commentator explains that the imam is obliged to divide the spoils and take out the khums (one-fifth) based on Quran 8:41. He also clarifies a detail: if a horse is killed after entering the enemy territory by someone, and its value is taken from the killer, that is part of the division. The text cuts off, but the ruling is clear regarding the shares.

Key Terms
الراجل (al-rajil): A foot soldier who fights on foot.
الفارس (al-faris): A horseman who fights on horseback.
البراذين (al-baradhīn): Mules and ponies; they are considered like horses for entitlement to a share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the division of spoils, a horseman fights with two horses. How many shares does he receive?
A) One share
B) Two shares
C) Three shares
D) Four shares

Key Takeaway
A foot soldier gets one share, a horseman gets two shares, and only horses and their equivalents qualify for an additional share.

Conditions for Granting al-Radkh to Slaves: The Permission Dispute
Explains who receives a small grant (radkh) instead of a full share in war booty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi views on granting radkh to a slave and apply the preferred (mufta bihi) view to a scenario.

Core Idea
For a slave to receive radkh, actual fighting suffices; master's permission is not required by istihsan.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on granting a small share of war booty (radkh) to slaves who participate in jihad. The source text reveals an intra-madhhab disagreement: does the slave need explicit permission from his master? We will analyze the arguments of al-Walwaliji and al-Sarakhsi and see which view is ultimately relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic categories for radkh
List the types of people mentioned in the text who may receive radkh: slaves, women, children, dhimmis. Note that radkh is a small grant, not a full share.
The text also mentions hired workers (ajir) who only get a share if they fight.
2
Isolate the condition for the slave
Read the passage on the slave. Al-Walwaliji requires two conditions: the slave must fight AND have his master's permission. Al-Sarakhsi argues that permission is not required by istihsan.
Focus on the phrase 'يرضخ له بشرطين: إذن المولى بالقتال له وأن يقاتل' vs. al-Sarakhsi's statement.
3
Understand the qiyas vs. istihsan reasoning
Al-Walwaliji's view relies on qiyas: the slave is not an independent fighter, so permission is needed. Al-Sarakhsi uses istihsan: the slave can earn, and fighting benefits the army, so he deserves radkh regardless of permission.
The text compares the case to a musta'min (safe-conduct seeker) who fights.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The difference is whether the slave receives anything. Under Walwaliji's view, a slave who fights without permission gets nothing. Under Sarakhsi's view, he gets radkh.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text leans toward Sarakhsi's view, and it is the position relied upon in later Hanafi fatawa. The slave receives radkh if he fights, even without the master's permission.
The tarjih authority is al-Sarakhsi in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرضخ في اللغة إعطاء القليل وهنا إعطاء القليل من سهم الغنيمة. وظاهر ما في المختصر يرضخ لهم مطلقاً وليس كذلك بل إنما يرضخ للعبد إذا قاتل لأنه دخل لخدمة المولى فصار كالتاجر والمرأة، وكذا الصبي بأن يكون له قدرة عليه. والمرأة إنما يرضخ لها إذا كانت تداوي الجرحى وتقوم على المرضى لأنها عاجزة عن حقيقة القتال فيقام هذا النوع من الإعانة مقام القتال بخلاف العبد لأنه قادر على حقيقة القتال؛ كذا في الهداية. وظاهره تخصيص هذا النوع من الإعانة وليس كذلك فقد قال الولوالجي : إن الإعانة منها قائمة مقام القتال كخدمة الغانمين وحفظ متاعهم .اهـ. وهو الحق كما لا يخفى والذمي إنما يرضخ له إذا قاتل أو دل على الطريق لأنه فيه منفعة للمسلمين إلا أنه يزاد على السهم في الدلالة إذا كانت فيه منفعة عظيمة، ولا يبلغ فيه السهم إذا قاتل لأنه جهاد والأول ليس من عمله فلا يسوى بينه وبين المسلم في حكم الجهاد ودل كلامهم على أنه يجوز الاستعانة بالكافر على القتال إذا دعت الحاجة إلى ذلك كما قدمناه وأطلق العبد فشمل المكاتب لقيام الرق وتوهم عجزه فيمنعه المولى عن القتال وقيد بالمذكورين لأن الأجير لا يسهم له ولا يرضخ لعدم اجتماع الأجر والنصيب من الغنيمة إلا إذا قاتل فإنه يسهم له كما قدمناه. وفي التتارخانية : لو أعتق العبد يرضخ له فيما أصيب من الغنيمة قبل عتقه والذمي المقاتل مع الإمام إذا أسلم يضرب له بسهم كامل فيما أصيب بعد إسلامه اهـ وظاهر ما في الولوالجية أن العبد يرضخ له بشرطين : إذن المولى بالقتال له وأن يقاتل . فعليه لو قاتل بلا إذن لا يرضخ له، ولم يذكر المصنف المجنون. وفي الولوالجية: ويرضخ للصبي والمجنون لأن السبب وجد في حقهما وهو القتال إلا أنهما تبع فصار كالعبد مع المولى اهـ . تستوجب النفقة على زوجها لأنها لا تصلح لخدمة الزوج والمريضة تستوجب لأنها كانت صالحة ولكن تعذر ذلك بعارض. قوله : (والذمي إنما يرضخ له إذا قاتل أو دل على الطريق) قال في الحواشي اليعقوبية : لا وجه لتخصيص حكم الدلالة على الطريق بالذمي لأن العبد أيضاً إذا دل يعطى له أجرة الدلالة بالغاً ما بلغ إلا أن يمنع إرادة التخصيص فليتأمل .اهـ. قوله : (إلا إذا قاتل فإنه يسهم له) أي بخلاف المذكورين فإنه يرضخ لهم إذا قاتلوا ولا يسهم قوله : وظاهر ما في الولوالجية أن العبد يرضخ له بشرطين (الخ وذلك حيث قال : العبد إذا كان مع مولاه يقاتل بإذن مولاه يرضخ له، وكذا الصبي والذمي والمرأة والمكاتب يرضخ لهم لأن العبد تبع للحر فإنه يقاتل بإذن المولى وأهل الذمة تبع للمسلمين، ولهذا لو أرادوا ينصبون راية لأنفسهم لا يمكنون والصبي تبع للرجل فلا تجوز التسوية بينهم في استحقاق الغنيمة وإن استووا في سبب الاستحقاق وهو القتال، وكان ينبغي أن لا بين الفرس وبين المالك لأنه تبع للمالك إلا أنا تركنا القياس بالنص ولا نص هنا، وإذا لم تجز التسوية يسهم له فيرضخ ولا يرضخ للعبد إن كان في خدمة مولاه ولا يقاتل اهـ. قلت: لكن قول الولوالجي : إذا كان مع مولاه يقاتل بإذن مولاه يرضخ له غير قيد بل يرضخ له وإن لم يكن بإذن المولى كما صرح به السرخسي في شرح السير الكبير وقال : إذا كان غير مأذون له بالقتال فلا شيء له قياساً لأنه ليس من أهل القتال فكان حاله كحال الحربي المستأمن إن قاتل بإذن الإمام استحق الرضخ وإلا فلا، وفي الاستحسان يرضخ له لأنه غير محجور عن الاكتساب وعما يتمحض منفعة وهو نظير القياس والاستحسان في العبد المحجور إذا أجر نفسه وسلم من العمل و به اندفع ما في الحواشي اليعقوبية من قوله إن العبد إذا كان مأذوناً بالقتال وقاتل ينبغي أن يكون له السهم الكامل كما لا يخفي اهـ .
And al-radkh in language is giving a little, and here it is giving a little from the share of the booty. The apparent meaning in al-Mukhtasar is that a grant is given to them absolutely, but it is not so. Rather, a grant is given to the slave if he fights, because he entered for the service of his master, so he becomes like the trader and the woman. Likewise, the boy if he has ability for it. The woman is given a grant if she treats the wounded and tends to the sick, because she is incapable of actual fighting, so this type of assistance stands in place of fighting, unlike the slave because he is capable of actual fighting. Thus in al-Hidayah. Its apparent meaning is the specification of this type of assistance, but it is not so. Al-Walwaliji said: Assistance from her stands in place of fighting, like serving the warriors and guarding their goods. End quote. It is the truth, as is not hidden. The dhimmi is given a grant only if he fights or guides on the road, because there is benefit for the Muslims in it, except that he is increased over the share in guidance if there is great benefit in it, and he does not reach the share if he fights because it is jihad, and the first is not from his action, so he is not equated with the Muslim in the ruling of jihad. Their speech indicates that it is permissible to seek help from the disbeliever in fighting if there is need for it, as we have presented. The slave is mentioned absolutely, so it includes the mukatib because slavery remains and the suspicion of his inability prevents the master from allowing him to fight. It is restricted to those mentioned because the hired worker is not given a share nor a grant because there cannot be both wage and share from booty, unless he fights, then he is given a share as we have presented. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: If a slave is freed, a grant is given to him for what is taken of booty before his emancipation. The dhimmi who fights with the Imam and then becomes Muslim is given a full share for what is taken after his Islam. End quote. The apparent meaning in al-Walwalijiyya is that a slave is given a grant with two conditions: permission of the master for fighting and that he fights. Therefore, if he fights without permission, he is not given a grant. The author did not mention the insane person. In al-Walwalijiyya: A grant is given to the boy and the insane person because the cause exists in their case, which is fighting, except that they are followers, so they become like the slave with the master. End quote. She is entitled to maintenance from her husband because she is not fit for the service of the husband, and the sick woman is entitled because she was fit but it became impossible due to an impediment. His statement: (And the dhimmi is given a grant only if he fights or guides on the road) Al-Hawashi al-Ya'qubiyya said: There is no basis for specifying the ruling of guiding on the road to the dhimmi, because the slave also, if he guides, is given the fee for guidance whatever it may be, unless specification is intended, so consider. End quote. His statement: (Except if he fights, then he is given a share) Meaning contrary to those mentioned, for they are given a grant if they fight, not a share. His statement: And the apparent meaning in al-Walwalijiyya that the slave is given a grant with two conditions (etc.) That is where he said: The slave, if he is with his master and fights with his master's permission, is given a grant. Likewise, the boy, the dhimmi, the woman, and the mukatib are given a grant because the slave is a follower of the free man, for he fights with the master's permission, and the people of dhimma are followers of the Muslims, and therefore if they wanted to set up a banner for themselves, they are not enabled. The boy is a follower of the man, so equality between them in entitlement to booty is not permissible, even if they are equal in the cause of entitlement, which is fighting. And it would be fitting that there be no difference between the horse and the owner because it is a follower of the owner, except that we abandoned analogy by text, and there is no text here. And since equality is not permissible, he is given a share? So he is given a grant. And the slave is not given a grant if he is in the service of his master and does not fight. End quote. I say: But the statement of al-Walwaliji: If he is with his master and fights with his master's permission, he is given a grant, is not restrictive; rather, he is given a grant even without the master's permission, as stated by al-Sarakhsi in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir, and he said: If he is not permitted to fight, then he gets nothing by analogy because he is not among the people of fighting, so his case is like the case of a musta'min (safe-conduct seeker) if he fights with the Imam's permission, he deserves the grant, otherwise not. By istihsan, he is given a grant because he is not prevented from earning and from what is purely beneficial. This is analogous to the analogy and istihsan in the case of a restricted slave who hires himself out and hands over the work. And with this, what is in al-Hawashi al-Ya'qubiyya is refuted, from his statement that if the slave is permitted to fight and fights, he should have the full share, as is not hidden. End quote.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a detailed commentary on the rulings of al-radkh—a small grant from war booty given to certain individuals who participate in jihad but are not fully entitled to a regular share (sahm). The author begins by defining radkh linguistically and legally. He then clarifies that radkh is not given absolutely to all mentioned in al-Mukhtasar; rather, conditions apply: a slave receives radkh only if he actually fights, because he enters battle in service to his master, not as a primary combatant, similar to a trader or a woman. A woman is given radkh if she provides auxiliary services like nursing, since she is incapable of fighting. A child receives radkh if he is capable of fighting. A dhimmi (protected non-Muslim) receives radkh if he fights or guides the Muslim army, but even if he fights, he does not receive a full share because jihad is specifically for Muslims. However, if a dhimmi converts during the campaign, he gets a full share for booty taken after his Islam. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the slave: according to al-Walwaliji, two conditions are required: the master's permission and actual fighting. However, al-Sarakhsi contends that even without the master's permission, istihsan (juristic preference) dictates that the slave should still receive radkh because he is not legally prevented from earning and his fighting provides benefit. The commentary also addresses the ruling for the insane and the boy, stating they receive radkh as followers. A misplaced sentence about a woman's maintenance (nafaqah) appears, likely a scribal error, which is best ignored in the context of war booty. Overall, the passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing analogy (qiyas) with istihsan and textual exceptions.

Key Terms
الرضخ (al-radkh): A small grant given to certain participants in jihad who are not entitled to a full share, such as slaves, women, children, and dhimmis.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): War booty taken from the enemy through force.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason such as public interest or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is required for a slave to receive radkh (small grant) from war booty?
A) Both the master's permission and actual fighting.
B) Only actual fighting; permission is not required.
C) Only the master's permission; fighting is not necessary.
D) Neither; slaves never receive radkh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, radkh is a discretionary grant for certain participants in jihad; for a slave, actual fighting suffices, and master's permission is not required by istihsan.

Priority of Poor Relatives in Khums Distribution
Ruling with proof on khums allocation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who receives khums and explain why poor relatives of the Prophet are prioritized over other eligible recipients.

Core Idea
Poor relatives of the Prophet take precedence in khums because sadaqah is forbidden to them; khums compensates.

The khums (one-fifth of war booty) is a sacred allocation mandated by the Quran. The Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and a key hadith, holds that the poor among the Prophet's relatives (Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib) are not merely equal recipients but are given priority over other categories. The rich relatives receive nothing. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: because sadaqah is prohibited for them, khums serves as their compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recipient categories
The text states that khums is for orphans, needy, and wayfarers, but immediately prioritizes 'dhu al-qurba' (poor relatives). List the three general categories and the special subcategory.
Dhu al-qurba refers to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib.
2
Locate the ruling on rich relatives
The passage explicitly says the rich have no share. Note this as a key Hanafi position: wealth disqualifies them despite kinship.
3
Analyse the primary proof: practice of the Caliphs
The text cites the four Rightly Guided Caliphs dividing khums into three shares (orphans, needy, wayfarers) with poor relatives given precedence. Recognise this as 'amal al-khulafa' al-rashidin, a strong source of law.
Al-Marghinani uses 'kafā bihim qadwah' (they suffice as an example).
4
Analyse the secondary proof: the hadith
The hadith states Allah dislikes for Banu Hashim the 'washings of people' (sadaqah) and compensates them with the fifth of the fifth. Understand the juridical link: compensation is only for those who would otherwise receive sadaqah, i.e., the poor.
Hadith from Muslim, Abu Dawood, etc.
5
Address potential objections
The passage considers two objections: (1) Why mention orphans separately if they already qualify via poverty? (2) Why mention relatives at all if they are subsumed under poverty? The answers clarify that the mention prevents misunderstandings about orphan or relative eligibility.
This is a classic usul exercise in bayan al-mujmal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والخمس لليتامى والمساكين وابن السبيل وقدم ذوو القربى الفقراء منهم عليهم ولا حق لأغنيائهم لأن الخلفاء الاربعة الراشدين رضي الله عنهم أجمعين قسموه على ثلاثة أسهم على نحو ما قلنا وكفى بهم قدوة. وقال عليه السلام يا معشر بني هاشم إن الله تعالى كره لكم غسالة الناس وأوساخهم وعوضكم منها بخمس الخمس»(۱) والعوض إنما يثبت في حق من يثبت في حقه المعوض وهم الفقراء، والنبي الله أعطاهم للنصرة ألا ترى أنه عليه السلام علل فقال : إنهم لم يزالوا معي هكذا في الجاهلية والإسلام وشبك بين أصابعه لأن المراد من النصر قرب النصرة لا قرب القرابة واليتيم صغير لا أب له فيدخل فقراء اليتامى من ذوي القربى في سهم اليتامى المذكورين دون أغنيائهم، والمسكين منهم في سهم المساكين وفقراء أبناء السبيل. فإن قيل : فلا فائدة حينئذ في ذكر اسم اليتيم حيث كان استحقاقه بالفقر والمسكنة لا باليتم أجيب بأن فائدته دفع توهم أن اليتيم لا يستحق من الغنيمة شيئاً لأن استحقاقها بالجهاد واليتيم صغير فلا يستحقها، ومثله ما ذكر في التأويلات للشيخ أبي لما كان فقراء ذوي القربي يستحقون بالفقر فلا فائدة في ذكرهم في القرآن. أجاب بأن أفهام بعض الناس قد تقتضي إلى أن الفقير منهم لا يستحق لأنه من قبيل الصدقة ولا تحل لهم، وفي الحاوى القدسي : وعن أبي يوسف أن الخمس يصرف لذوي القربى واليتامى والمساكين أسهم : سهم (۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الزكاة حديث ١٦٧، ١٦٨ . أبو داود في كتاب الإمارة باب ٢٠. النسائي في كتاب الزكاة باب ٩٥ الموطأ في كتاب الصدقة حديث ۱۳، ١٥ أحمد في مسنده (٤٠٢/٣) (٤/ (١٦٦
His statement: (And the fifth is for the orphans, the needy, and the wayfarer, and the poor relatives are given precedence over them, and their rich have no right, because the four Rightly Guided Caliphs, may Allah be pleased with them all, divided it into three shares in the manner we have said, and they are sufficient as an example. And he, peace be upon him, said: 'O assembly of Banu Hashim, indeed Allah the Exalted dislikes for you the washings of people and their filth, and He has compensated you with the fifth of the fifth.' And compensation only exists for the one for whom the compensated right exists, and they are the poor. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, gave them for support (nusrah). Do you not see that he, peace be upon him, gave the reason saying: 'They have always been with me like this in Jahiliyyah and Islam' and he interlaced his fingers, because what is meant by support is closeness of support, not closeness of kinship. And the orphan is a young child with no father, so the poor orphans from among the relatives enter into the share of the aforementioned orphans, excluding their rich. And the needy among them enter into the share of the needy, and the poor wayfarers. If it is said: Then what is the benefit of mentioning the name 'orphan' when his entitlement is due to poverty and need, not orphanhood? The answer is that its benefit is to repel the supposition that the orphan is not entitled to anything from booty because entitlement is by jihad, and the orphan is young, so he is not entitled. And similar is what is mentioned in al-Ta'wilat of Shaykh Abi Mansur: Since the poor relatives are entitled due to poverty, there is no benefit in mentioning them in the Quran. He answered: The understanding of some people might lead them to think that the poor among them are not entitled because it is a kind of charity (sadaqah) and it is not permissible for them. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: And from Abu Yusuf that the fifth is spent on the relatives, orphans, and needy.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the distribution of the khums (one-fifth of war booty) as prescribed in the Quran (Surah al-Anfal 8:41). The author explains that the khums is divided into three shares: for orphans, the needy, and wayfarers, but specifies that the poor relatives of the Prophet (Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib) are given priority and take precedence over these categories. The rich relatives have no claim, as established by the practice of the four Rightly Guided Caliphs and a hadith in which the Prophet said that Allah has compensated them with the khums in lieu of sadaqah (charity), which is forbidden to them. The passage addresses a potential objection: if relatives are included in the general categories of orphans, needy, and wayfarers, then why mention them separately? The answer is to remove the misconception that orphans and relatives have no right to booty at all, since entitlement is through jihad, which they may not have performed. The text also cites a narration from Abu Yusuf that the khums is spent on relatives, orphans, and needy in general, implying that the poor relatives are subsumed under the other categories. Overall, the Hanafi position is that the khums is not distributed to the rich of Banu Hashim; only the poor among them receive it, and they are given priority over other poor recipients.

Key Terms
الخمس (al-khums): One-fifth of war booty set aside for specified recipients: orphans, the needy, wayfarers, and poor relatives of the Prophet.
ذو القربى (dhu al-qurba): Relatives of the Prophet, specifically Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, who are prohibited from receiving sadaqah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are the poor relatives of the Prophet given priority in the distribution of khums over other recipients?
A) Because of their noble lineage
B) Because sadaqah is forbidden to them and khums compensates for that
C) Because they fought in jihad
D) Because they are always poor

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the poor of Banu Hashim in khums distribution because they are compensated for the prohibition of sadaqah, while the rich have no claim.

Spoils and Khums: The Role of Strength (Man'ah)
Determining khums on spoils based on strength and permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that spoils taken by force (ghanimah) are subject to khums, distinguishing between groups with and without strength (man'ah) and with or without the imam's permission.

Core Idea
Spoils taken by force are ghanimah; khums applies even without permission if the group is strong.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies when spoils taken by a group of Muslims entering enemy territory without the imam's permission are subject to khums. The key determining factor is the group's strength (man'ah) — their ability to dominate by force. This distinction affects the obligation of khums and the classification of the spoils as ghanimah versus ikhtilas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a group of Muslims entering enemy territory and seizing property. The ruling varies: if the group has man'ah (strength), khums is wajib on the spoils; if weak, no khums.
The spoils of a strong group are considered ghanimah; weak group's seizure is ikhtilas (theft).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the definition of ghanimah: property taken by force (qahr) and domination (ghalaba). The text contrasts this with ikhtilas (stealth). The presence of force is the criterion.
The definition is derived from the linguistic meaning of ghanimah, which implies overcoming the enemy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The critical element is the presence of force. A strong group exerts force, so their seizure fits the definition of ghanimah; a weak group does not, so their seizure is ikhtilas, not ghanimah.
The force must be sufficient to dominate the enemy, not merely any taking.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
For a weak group that enters with the imam's permission, there are two narrations: one says no khums (since they lack force), the mashhur says khums because the imam's permission implies his commitment to support them, effectively giving them strength.
The mashhur view is that khums applies with permission even if weak.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that with the imam's permission, khums is always wajib; without permission, only the strong group is subject to khums. The imam can waive khums for a weak group but not for a strong group.
This tarjih is from al-Muhit and supported by the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن دخل جمع ذوو منعة دارهم بلا إذن خمس ما أخذوا وإلا لا) أي وإن لم يكونوا ذوي منعة لا يخمس لأن الغنيمة هو المأخوذ قهراً وغلبة لا اختلاساً وسرقة والخمس وظيفتها والقهر موجود في الأول والاختلاس في الثاني، ولا يضر كونه بغير إذن الإمام لأنه يجب عليه أن ينصرهم إذ لو خذلهم كان فيه وهن بالمسلمين بخلاف الواحد والاثنين لا يجب عليه نصرتهم. والتقييد بغير إذن الإمام ليس احترازياً لأنه لو كان بإذن الإمام ولهم منعة فإنه يخمس بالأولى، ولو لم يكن له منعة كواحد أو اثنين دخل بإذن الإمام ففيه روايتان، والمشهور أنه يخمس لأنه لما أذن لهم الإمام فقد التزم نصرتهم بالأمداد فصار كالمنعة. فالحاصل أن الداخل بإذن الإمام يخمس ما أخذه مطلقاً وبغير إذنه، فإن كان ذا منعة خمس وإلا لا. وفي المحيط : لو قال الإمام ما أصبتم فهو لكم لا خمس فيه فإن كانوا لا منعة لهم جاز، وإن كان لهم منعة لا يجوز لأن الخمس في الأول واجب بقول الإمام فله أن يبطله بقوله بخلافه في الثاني ولذا لو دخلوا بغير إذنه خمس ما أخذوه
His statement: (And if a group with strength enters their home without permission, then khums is taken on what they seized; otherwise no). That is, if they are not of strength, it is not khumsed, because ghanimah is what is taken by force and domination, not by stealth and theft. And khums is its function, and force exists in the first, and stealth in the second. And it is not harmful that it is without the Imam's permission, because he is obligated to support them, for if he abandoned them, there would be weakness in the Muslims, unlike the case of one or two individuals, where he is not obligated to support them. And the restriction to 'without the Imam's permission' is not exclusive, because if it were with the Imam's permission and they had strength, then it is khumsed a fortiori. And if they have no strength, like one or two individuals, entering with the Imam's permission, there are two narrations; the well-known one is that it is khumsed, because when the Imam permitted them, he undertook to support them with reinforcements, so it becomes like having strength. So the conclusion is that one who enters with the Imam's permission has his spoils khumsed absolutely; and without his permission, if he has strength, it is khumsed; otherwise not. And in al-Muhit: If the Imam says 'Whatever you seize is yours, no khums on it,' then if they have no strength, it is permissible; if they have strength, it is not permissible, because khums in the first is obligatory by the Imam's word, so he can invalidate it by his word, unlike in the second case. Therefore, if they entered without his permission, their spoils are khumsed.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a group of Muslims who enter enemy territory without the imam's permission and seize spoils. The key factor is whether the group has 'man'ah' (strength/numerical power to dominate). If they do, their spoils are considered ghanimah (war booty) and thus subject to khums (one-fifth tax). If they lack strength, the seizure is considered ikhtilas (stealth) or sariqah (theft), not ghanimah, so no khums. The proof is that ghanimah is defined as property taken by force (qahr) and domination (ghalaba). The lack of imam's permission does not exempt them because the imam is obligated to support them to avoid weakening Muslims; this obligation does not apply to a small group of one or two. The condition 'without permission' is not restrictive: if they had permission and strength, khums is applied even more so. If they are weak but have permission, there are two narrations; the relied-upon (mashhur) view is that it is khumsed because the imam's permission implies his commitment to support them, making them effectively strong. The author summarizes: with permission: always khums; without permission: khums only if strong. There is also a discussion in al-Muhit where the imam can waive khums for a weak group by saying 'it's yours,' but he cannot waive it for a strong group because khums becomes wajib by his word, but in the strong case it is wajib by sharia.

Key Terms
المنعة (al-man'ah): Strength or power to overcome the enemy; a group that can dominate by force.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Property taken from the enemy by force and domination in a military context.
الاختلاس (al-ikhtilas): Taking property stealthily, without domination; this is not ghanimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A group of 12 Muslims without permission enters enemy territory and seizes property by force. Which ruling applies?
A) No khums because they lacked permission
B) Khums is wajib because they had man'ah
C) Khums is wajib only if the imam later approves
D) The spoils are halal for the group since they took from enemies

Key Takeaway
Khums on spoils depends on whether the seizure was by force (ghanimah) — determined by the group's strength (man'ah) — not merely on the imam's permission.

The Imam's Authority to Grant Nafal and the Ruling of Tahrid
Explaining imam's right to grant nafal and tahrid's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's discretion in granting nafal and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on whether tahrid (incitement) is recommended (mandub) or obligatory (wajib).

Core Idea
The imam may grant nafal as an incentive to soldiers; the debate is whether tahrid itself is mandub or wajib.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq clarifies that the imam has the authority to promise extra spoils to soldiers before battle, based on the practice of the Rightly-Guided Caliphs. It also highlights a difference within the Hanafi school regarding the legal classification of incitement (tahrid): some scholars consider it recommended (mandub), while others consider it obligatory (wajib).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the ruling on granting nafal. The text states 'the imam may grant nafal' – this indicates permissibility (ibāḥah).
The imam's authority is discretionary, not a fixed entitlement.
2
Understand the condition for nafal
Note that nafal is granted from the spoils after the khums has been set aside. The text says 'after paying the khums'. This is a condition for its validity.
Some copies read 'after paying the khums' (بعدما دفع الخمس) while others omit 'ma' – the meaning is the same.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on tahrid
The author cites a disagreement: al-Hidayah states that incitement (tahrid) is mandub (recommended), while al-Fath argues it is wajib (obligatory) based on a Quranic text. This is a legitimate difference within the school regarding the strength of the command.
The mufta bihi remains that the imam may grant nafal; incitement is at least recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وللإمام أن ينفل بقوله من قتل قتيلاً فله ويقدمون ولا يدفع لأغنيائهم شيء. وعن أبي يوسف الخ. إذ لو كان كما قاله في أبي يوسف عين ما قبلها قوله : (والحجة عليه ما قدمناه أي من أن الخلفاء الراشدين إنما اقتسموا الخمس على ثلاثة، فلو كان كما ذكر لقسموه على أربعة ورفعوا سهمه لأنفسهم؛ كذا في الفتح. قوله : (أي بعدما دفع الخمس كذا في النسخ والذي في الفتح بدون «ما» وهو أظهر قوله: (لأن التحريض مندوبة إليه كذا وقع في الهداية قال في الفتح واعلم أن التحريض واجب للنص المذكور
His statement: (And the Imam may grant nafal by his saying: 'Whoever kills an enemy, it is for him' and they advance, and nothing is given to their rich. And from Abu Yusuf etc. For if it were as he said in Abu Yusuf, it would be the same as before. His statement: (And the proof against him is what we have presented) i.e., that the Rightly-Guided Caliphs divided the khums into three; if it were as he mentioned, they would have divided it into four and taken his share for themselves. As in al-Fath. His statement: (i.e., after paying the khums) as in the copies, and what is in al-Fath without 'ma' and it is more apparent. His statement: (Because incitement is recommended) as occurred in al-Hidayah. He said in al-Fath: And know that incitement is obligatory due to the mentioned text.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage discusses the imam's authority to grant nafal (additional reward from spoils) to soldiers as an incentive before battle. The imam can say 'whoever kills an enemy gets his spoils.' This is a sunnah practice. The text then returns to the earlier dispute with al-Shafi'i, repeating that the Caliphs' practice of dividing khums into three disproves the Shafi'i view that the Prophet's share goes to the caliph. The author also clarifies a textual variant: the phrase 'after paying the khums' in some copies versus without 'ma' in al-Fath. Finally, the author notes that in al-Hidayah it says 'incitement is recommended (mandubah)', but al-Fath says incitement is obligatory (wajib) based on a text (the Quranic verse about fighting).

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafal): Additional reward granted by the imam from the spoils to encourage bravery before a battle.
التحريض (al-tahrid): Incitement to fight, which may be done by promising nafal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the imam granting nafal (additional reward) to soldiers before battle?
A) It is wajib
B) It is permissible (mubah)
C) It is haram
D) It is only for the rich

Key Takeaway
The imam has the discretionary authority to grant nafal from spoils after khums before battle; the status of tahrid (incitement) is debated within the school as mandub or wajib.

8 min
The Prophet's Share and Safiy: Abrogated After Death
Ruling on Prophet's share and safiy post-death with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Prophet's share and safiy after his death, explain the reasoning, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position on the caliph's entitlement.

Core Idea
The Prophet's exclusive share from khums ceased with his prophethood; the caliphs' practice confirmed its abrogation.

This lesson addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the distribution of khums (one-fifth of war booty) after the death of the Prophet ﷺ. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, holds that the Prophet's share (sahm al-nabi) and his personal selection (al-safiy) are both dropped. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, argues that the share should be given to the caliph as the head of state. We will examine the textual evidence and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The disputed issue is whether the Prophet's share of khums and the safiy continue after his death or are abrogated.
The key term is 'sahm al-nabi' — the one-fifth portion of khums allocated to the Prophet.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi ruling: both the share and safiy are dropped (yasqutu). The proof: the Prophethood (risala) was the cause (sabab) for entitlement, and after his death no recipient remains. Furthermore, the caliphs (Abu Bakr, 'Umar, etc.) when distributing khums omitted the Prophet's share, dividing it into three parts (orphans, poor, wayfarers) per Quran 59:7. Their consensus (ijma) is probative.
The text also mentions that safiy is similar (ka al-safiy) in ruling.
3
Present the Shafi'i counter-position
Al-Shafi'i held that the Prophet's share should be spent on the caliph (yusraf ila al-khalifa), arguing that the share is for the head of state and that the caliph is the successor.
The source text does not elaborate al-Shafi'i's full proof, but the dispute is recorded.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i view
The Hanafi refutation (al-hujja 'alayhi ma qaddamnahu) refers to the earlier evidence: the practice of the caliphs, who were the most knowledgeable about the Sunnah, and who did not take the share. This establishes that the share was not meant for the ruler after the Prophet.
The Hanafi argument is based on 'amal (practice) of the sahaba, which is a strong proof.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects how khums is distributed. In the Hanafi school, khums is divided into three categories (yatama, masakin, ibn al-sabil) per Quran 59:7. In the Shafi'i school, there is a fourth category: the share of the head of state (sahm al-imam). This has implications for state treasury and wartime funds.
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that the share is completely dropped.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وسهم النبي عليه السلام سقط بموته كالصفى لأن النبي لو كان يستحقه برسالته ولا رسول بعده والصفي شيء كان النبي عليه السلام يصطفيه لنفسه من الغنيمة مثل درع أو سيف أو جارية . وقال الشافعي رضي الله عنه : يصرف سهم الرسول الله إلى الخليفة والحجة عليه ما قدمناه .
His statement: (And the share of the Prophet, peace be upon him, is dropped with his death, like the safiy, because the Prophet used to deserve it by his prophethood, and there is no messenger after him. The safiy is something that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to select for himself from the booty, such as a coat of mail, a sword, or a slave-girl.) And al-Shafi‘i, may Allah be pleased with him, said: The share of the Messenger of Allah is to be spent on the caliph. The proof against him is what we have presented earlier.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and an inter-madhhab dispute. The text states that the Prophet's share (sahm al-rasul) and his personal selection (safiy) both cease upon his death. The reasoning: the Prophet's right to these was due to his prophethood, and since there is no prophet after him, there is no recipient. The safiy was a special item he took for himself before distribution. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, arguing that the share should go to the caliph (successor). The Hanafi refutation (al-hujja 'alayhi ma qaddamnahu) refers to the practice of the rightly-guided caliphs who distributed the khums among only three categories (orphans, poor, wayfarers), omitting the Prophet's share. This shows it was abrogated.

Key Terms
سهم النبي (sahm al-nabi): The one-fifth of the khums allocated to the Prophet for his own use during his lifetime.
الصفي (al-safiy): An item the Prophet selected from the booty before distribution, such as a sword or a slave-girl.
الخمس (al-khums): One-fifth of war booty (ghanima) and certain other gains, set aside for specific recipients as per Quran 8:41 and 59:7.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the Prophet's share (sahm al-rasul) of the khums after his death?
A) It is given to the caliph.
B) It is dropped entirely.
C) It is given to the poor and needy only.
D) It is kept for future prophets.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's share and safiy are uniquely linked to his prophethood and thus cease with his death; the caliphs' practice confirms this, distinguishing the Hanafi ruling from the Shafi'i view.

The Default Ruling: Salb is Ghanimah, Not Exclusive to the Killer
This passage opens with the default ruling on salb and provides two hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi default ruling on the slain's spoils (salb) and explain how the hadith 'man qatala qatilan falahu salabuhu' is reconciled with the principle that all spoils are ghanimah.

Core Idea
Salb is part of ghanimah unless the Imam grants it as tanfil; the killer has no automatic right.

In battle, spoils taken from a slain enemy raise the question: does the killer get them exclusively? The Hanafi school holds that all spoils, including what is on the slain, are part of the ghanimah (booty) to be divided among the army. The prophetic hadith that seems to give the killer the spoils is interpreted as a discretionary grant (tanfil) by the Imam, not as a fixed right. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the legal reasoning behind this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Default Ruling
The text states: 'The spoils belong to all if he did not grant (tanfil).' This means the killer is not automatically entitled; it goes into the general booty.
The default is division as ghanimah.
2
Examine the First Proof
The Prophet said to Habib ibn Abi Salamah: 'You have nothing from the spoils of your slain except what your Imam willingly gives you.' This directly denies an automatic right.
This is a clear textual proof against entitlement.
3
Interpret the Second Hadith
The hadith 'Whoever kills a slain, he gets his spoils' is cited. The text explains it could mean a prescribed share (nasb al-shar') or a discretionary grant (tanfil). They choose tanfil to reconcile with the first hadith.
The reconciling interpretation is tanfil.
4
Connect to Usul al-Fiqh
The interpretive move uses the principle of reconciling conflicting texts (al-jam' wa al-tawfiq). The second hadith is taken to indicate permissibility (ibaha) rather than obligation (wujub), because of the first hadith and the collective nature of ghanimah.
This is a standard Hanafi usul method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظاهر ما في الذخيرة عدم الحرمة قوله : (والسلب للكل إن لم ينفل) أي لا يختص به القاتل عندنا لأنه مأخوذ بقوة الجيش فيكون غنيمة فيقسم بينهم قسمة الغنائم كما نطق به النص وقال عليه السلام الحبيب بن أبي سلمة ليس لك من سلب قتيلك إلا ما طابت به نفس إمامك. وأما قوله عليه السلام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه» (۱) فيحتمل نصب الشرع ويحتمل التنفيل فنحمله على الثاني لما روينا قوله : (وهو) مركبه وثيابه وسلاحه وما معه) أي السلب ما ذكر للعرف. وفي المغرب : السلب المسلوب وعن الليث والأزهري : كل ما على الإنسان من اللباس فهو سلب وللفقهاء فيه كلام .اهـ. وفي القاموس السلب بالتحريك ما يسلب وجمعه أسلاب ودخل في مركبه ما كان عليه من سرج وآلة وما مع المقتول شامل لما كان في وسطه أو على دابته وما عدا ذلك مما هو مع غلامه أو في بيته أو في خيمته فليس بسلب. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان السلب عند المشرك عارية من صبي أو امرأة لأنه يستغنم مالهما كمال البالغ، وما إذا كان السلب ملكاً لمسلم دخل دارهم بأمان فغصبه المشرك المقتول لأنه ملكه بالاستيلاء فانقطع ملك المسلم عنه . ولو أخذ المشركون سلب المقتول ثم انهزموا فهو غنيمة ولا شيء للقاتل لأنهم ملكوه بالاستيلاء فبطل ملك القاتل ثم ملكه الغزاة وإن لم يدر أنهم أخذوه، فإن كان منزوعاً عنه فهو فيء لإثبات يدهم عليه بالنزع وإلا فهو للقاتل وإن جره المشركون أو حملوه على دابته وعليها سلاحه بخلاف ما إذا حملوا أسلحتهم وأمتعتهم عليها فإنه فيء. ولو وجد على دابة بعدما سار العسكر مرحلة أو مرحلتين ولا يدري أكان أحد في يد أو لا فهو للقاتل قياساً لا استحساناً ولو قال من قتل قتيلاً فله فرسه فقتل راجل راجلاً ومع غلامه فرسه قائم بجنبه بين الصفين يكون للقاتل فرسه إذا كان فرسه مع . غلامه بقرب منه لأن مقصود الإمام قتل من كان متمكناً من القتال فارساً وهذا كذلك، وإن لم يكن بجنبه في الصف فلا يكون له. ولو قتل مشركاً على برذون كان له لأنه يسمى فارساً، ولو كان على حمار أو بغل أو حمل لا يستحق السلب لأن راكب هذه الأشياء لا فارساً ولذا لا يسمى يستحق سهم الفارس؛ كذا في المحيط وبه علم أن ما ذكره الشارح عن المحيط بأنه قال الإمام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه سبق قلم، وإنما المذكور في المحيط فله فرسه والدليل عليه أنه ينبغي أن يباع السلاح منهم وقول المتن في الأيمان ومن حلف على معصية ينبغي أن يحنث) شائع في كلامهم قوله : (سبق (قلم قال الرملي : أي من بعض النساخ والذي في نسخنا من الزيلعي فله فرسه كما في المحيط (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب المفازي باب .٥٤ مسلم في كتاب الجهاد حديث ٤٢. أبو داود في كتاب الجهاد باب ١٣٦. الترمذي في كتاب السير باب ۱۳ . الموطأ في كتاب الجهاد حديث ١٨. أحمد في مسنده (١٢/٥، ٢٩٥) قال آخراً: لو كان راكباً على بغل ونحوه لا يكون له ولو كان التنفيل بلفظ السلب لاستحقه لأن المركب أعم منه ومن الفرس. قال في القاموس : المركب كمقعد واحد مراكب البر والبحر اهـ. وفي الهداية ثم حكم التنفيل قطع حق الباقين فأما الملك فإنما يثبت بعد الإحراز بدار الإسلام لما مر من قبل حتى لو قال الأمير من أصاب جارية فهي له فأصابها مسلم فاستبرأها لم يجز له وطؤها وكذا لا يبيعها هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد له أن يطاها ويبيعها لأن التنفيل يثبت به الملك عنده كما يثبت بالقسمة في دار الحرب والشراء من الحربي ووجوب الضمان بالإتلاف قد قيل على هذا الاختلاف اهـ. والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
That which is apparent in al-Dhakhira is that there is no prohibition. His statement: (And the spoils (salb) belong to all if he did not grant (tanfil)) meaning the killer is not exclusively entitled to it according to us because it is taken by the strength of the army, so it becomes booty (ghanimah) and is divided among them like the division of booty, as the text (Quran) declares. And the Prophet ﷺ said to Habib ibn Abi Salamah: 'You have nothing from the spoils of your slain except what your Imam willingly gives you.' As for his statement ﷺ: 'Whoever kills a slain, he gets his spoils' – it could mean a prescribed share (nasb al-shar') or it could mean an extra grant (tanfil). We interpret it as the second based on what we narrated. His statement: (And it is his mount, clothes, weapon, and what is with him) i.e., al-salb is what was mentioned according to custom. In al-Mughrib: al-salb is the plundered goods. From al-Layth and al-Azhari: everything on a person of clothing is salb, but jurists have discussion about it. In al-Qamus: al-salb (with fath of the letter sin) is what is plundered, plural aslāb. Included in 'his mount' is what is on it of saddle and equipment, and 'what is with the slain' includes what was on his belt or on his animal. Anything else that is with his servant or in his house or tent is not salb. It is unrestricted, so it includes if the salb was with the polytheist as a loan from a child or woman, because their property is taken as booty like that of an adult. And if the salb was the property of a Muslim who entered their land with aman and the slain polytheist seized it, it becomes the polytheist's property by seizure, cutting off the Muslim's ownership. If the polytheists took the salb of the slain and then were defeated, it is booty and the killer gets nothing, because they owned it by seizure, so the killer's ownership is nullified, then the warriors own it, even if they don't know that they took it. If it was stripped from him, it is fay’ because they established their hand on it by stripping; otherwise it is for the killer. If the polytheists dragged or carried him on his animal with his weapons on it, it is different from if they carried their own weapons and belongings on it, which would be fay’. If something is found on an animal after the army has traveled one or two stages, and it is unknown whether anyone had it in hand or not, it belongs to the killer by qiyas, not istihsan. If someone says 'whoever kills a slain, he gets his horse', and a foot soldier kills a foot soldier while his servant has his horse standing near him between the ranks, the killer gets the horse if the horse was near his servant, because the Imam's intent is to kill one who is capable of fighting as a horseman, and this is so. But if it was not near him in the ranks, he does not get it. If he kills a polytheist on a baridhun (strong horse), he gets it because he is called a horseman. If he was on a donkey, mule, or ram, he does not deserve the salb because the rider of these things is not a horseman and thus does not deserve the horseman's share. In al-Muhit: thus it is known that what the commentator mentioned from al-Muhit that the Imam said 'whoever kills a slain gets his salb' is a slip of the pen; what is mentioned in al-Muhit is 'gets his horse'. Evidence is that the weapons should be sold from them. And the statement of the text in al-Ayman: 'whoever swears to commit a sin should break his oath' is common in their speech. His statement: (slip of the pen) – al-Ramli said: 'from some scribes, and in our copies from al-Zayla'i it is 'gets his horse' as in al-Muhit.' Narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Muwatta', Ahmad... He said further: if he was riding a mule or similar, he does not get it; but if the grant (tanfil) was worded as 'salb', he would deserve it because 'mount' (markab) is more general than horse. Al-Qamus says: al-markab (like masjad) refers to one of the mounts of land and sea. In al-Hidayah: then the ruling of tanfil is that it cuts off the right of others. As for ownership, it is only established after transport to dar al-Islam, as previously mentioned. So if the amir says 'whoever gets a slave girl, she is his', and a Muslim gets her and then performs istibra', he may not have intercourse with her, nor sell her according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said he may have intercourse and sell her because, according to him, tanfil establishes ownership, just as ownership is established by division in dar al-harb and purchase from a harbi, and the obligation of guarantee for destruction is said to differ based on this difference. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the rules of al-salb (spoils taken from a slain enemy) and al-tanfil (extra grants by the Imam). The commentator begins by citing al-Dhakhira that there is no prohibition (apparently referring to a previous issue). The main ruling: the salb belongs to the entire army, not exclusively to the killer, because it is obtained through the collective strength of the army, thus it is ghanimah divided among all. This is supported by the hadith where the Prophet told Habib ibn Abi Salamah that he only gets what the Imam gives him. The hadith 'Whoever kills a slain, he gets his spoils' is interpreted as referring to tanfil (a discretionary grant), not as a fixed right, to reconcile with the first hadith. The commentator then defines salb: according to custom, it includes the slain's mount, clothes, weapons, and what he carries. He cites various lexicons: al-Mughrib, al-Layth, al-Azhari, and al-Qamus. He elaborates: the mount includes its saddle and equipment; 'what is with the slain' includes what is on his belt or animal. Anything with his servant, in his house, or tent is not salb. The rule applies whether the salb was borrowed from a child or woman, as their property is also booty. If the salb was originally a Muslim's property seized by the slain polytheist, it becomes the polytheist's property by seizure, so the killer does not get it. If the polytheists take the salb from the slain and then flee, the salb becomes general booty, not for the killer, because the polytheists had owned it by seizure. If the polytheists stripped the slain of his salb, it becomes fay' (property of the state). If they dragged him or his animal, the rider's possessions are for the killer, but their own weapons on the animal are fay'. If a salb is found on an animal after the army has moved one or two stages, it goes to the killer by qiyas (analogy) but not by istihsan (juristic preference). The text then addresses a specific case: if the Imam says 'whoever kills gets his horse', and a foot soldier kills a foot soldier whose horse is nearby with his servant, the killer gets the horse if it is close. If not, he doesn't. Killing a polytheist on a strong horse (bardhun) gives entitlement to the horse because he is a horseman; but on a donkey, mule, or ram, no. The commentator corrects a scribal error: 'salba' should be 'farasahu' (his horse) as in al-Muhit. The passage then discusses al-tanfil: it cuts off the right of others to the grant. Ownership under tanfil is only established after transport to dar al-Islam. There is an ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf say that if the Imam grants a slave girl, the recipient cannot have intercourse or sell her until after transport, because ownership is not yet complete. Muhammad says he can, as tanfil establishes immediate ownership in dar al-harb, similar to division or purchase.

Key Terms
السلب (al-salb): The spoils taken from a slain enemy, specifically his mount, weapons, and what he carries as per custom.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Booty taken from the enemy by force, to be divided among the army after one-fifth is set aside.
التنفيل (al-tanfil): An extra grant from the Imam to a warrior beyond the regular share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, why is the hadith 'man qatala qatilan falahu salabuhu' interpreted as tanfil rather than as a fixed right?
A) Because the hadith is weak.
B) Because it conflicts with the hadith to Habib that denies the killer's right, so they reconcile by interpreting it as a permission for the Imam.
C) Because the Quranic verse on ghanimah abrogates it.
D) Because the Hanafi school does not accept the hadith.

Key Takeaway
The default Hanafi position is that the slain's spoils belong to the army as booty, and the killer has no automatic right unless the Imam grants it as tanfil.
